Conclusion
Conclusion
8.0.2
Failure mode
The collapse mode provided by Nucleus is in general found to provide a good estimate
of the failure mode, disregarding the specimens where the failure mode was governed
by crunching at the support. When the failure load for two diﬀerent mechanism is
governed by almost the same load level, it can be diﬃcult to determine the failure
mechanisms by only consider the animated collapse mod. However by considering
the stresses/forces in the model, the can easily be determined. In the cases, where
this was relevant, the failure mode is found to be govern by the same mechanism as
found by the experiments. From consideration of the stresses provided by Nucleus in
ULS, the principal direction were found to be almost identical to the crack pattern
at failure for the deep beams. Thus, it may be concluded that the stress distribution
provided by Nuclues complies with the actual stress distribution for the specimens
at failure. This furthermore indicates that the stress ﬁeld provided by the lower
bound solution gives rather good estimate, of the structures ability to redistribute
the stresses, simulating the exact distribution at failure.
8.0.3
Serviceability limit state
The stress in the reinforcement for the T-beams were found to depend on cracks
developing crossing the stirrups.
The stirrups stresses determined by analytical
calculation using the complimentary energy and the elastic stresses determined by
Nucleus (also considering complimentary energy) is almost the same. Both solutions
is found to be parallel to the stirrup forces, but with a horizontal translation K which
is found to variate depending on the reinforcement ration.
The tensile strength of the concrete is found to correspond with the eﬀective ten-
sile strength determined by the eﬀectiveness factor ν = 0.5 and by determined the
tensile strength depended of the concrete strength √0.1fc and not from tensile test,
however at leas not by use of ν = 0.5. If the tensile strength is determined from
tensile test, the eﬀective strength may be determined by use of ν = 0.37.
Considering the redistribution of the stresses θe −θp found by Nucleus, a clear re-
lation between the reinforcement degree and the rotation of the stresses, from the
cracked elastic state to the ultimate limit state is found. The relations corresponding
to; when the beam becomes more ductile (the amount of reinforcement is enhanced)
the need for redistribution of the stresses gets minimized. However when the speci-
men becomes over-reinforced Φ
ν > 0.5 it is not quite possible to predict the relation
between the distribution of stresses and, the reinforcement ratio.
Analysing the load level where service load might occur corresponding 0.5−0.6Pmax,
it its found that the stirrups have not yet yielded in the experiments, due to the
horizontal translation caused by the tensile strength of the concrete. However, the
solution provided by Nucleus will assume yield of the reinforcement before it actually
does because the program neglects the tensile strength of the program. Hence, it
is safe to use the solution provided by Nucleus predicting when yielding will occur.
Department of Civil Engineering - Technical University of Denmark
109
==PAGE:124==
8.1.
Future studies
Conclusion
However, the rotation the stress ﬁled has to be undertaking in order to go from the
elastic range to the plastic state, is the same for the Nucleus and the Experiment
(with or without tensile strength of the concrete).
Comparing the direction of the principal stresses for the high beams with the crack
pattern found by the tests it can be concluded, that stress determine represents the
reality of the stress distribution in the beam, and that it in fact will be possible to
predict the crack patten from the direction of the principle stresses. The crack will
occur in the same direction as the second principal direction and perpendicular to
the ﬁrst principle direction. This furthermore indicates that the stress ﬁeld provided
by the lower bound solution gives rather good estimates of the structures ability to
redistributes the stresses, simulating the exact distribution at failure, even though
the requirements is not satisﬁed to the minimum reinforcement. Thus using Nucleus
to minimize the amount of reinforcement by use of the optimized lower bound solu-
tion still provides a safe design in the serviceability limit state.
Hence it may therefore be concluded, that even though the optimized lower bound
solution allows low reinforcement degrees and allow us to optimize the design of the
structure, Nucleus is able to provide a good estimate of the elements behaviour in
the cracked elastic sate and the ultimate limed state. However it is important to
keep in mind, that even though the program allows us to calculation complicate
structural elements it still requires a lot of knowledge from the engineer in order to
provide a correct numerical model for the individual elements, keeping in mind the
challenges faced in this report, modelling these relative "simple" cases. Especially in
the case of statically undetermined structures and even more if openings are present
in the structure.
8.1
Future studies
From the investigations done in this report it is conﬁrmed that the failure envelop
implemented in Nucleus agrees rather well, with experiments from the literature.
The program is also found to provide a rather good estimate of the distribution
and redistribution of the stresses i.e predicting the ductility of the structure. This
provides a good basis for expanding the program to also include calculation of crack
width in the future. However, the ﬁrst step will be to implement the ridged material
in the serviceability limit state calculation, and perform a comparison of the stresses
in the reinforcement in the elastic range for the simple supported deep beams and
the continuous deep beams with web openings, as was done for the T-beams in this
report.

Appendix B
T-beams
In this appendix is collected all the calculation sheets in relation to analyse of the
T-beams. The main results are summarized in Table B.1 and B.2 followed by a
calculation sheet for each beam analysing the angle, determine the shear capacity
and the moment capacity.
